Telecommunications Special Issue

Voices of the Telecommunications World: Japan Expert vs. Italy Expert

— Lü Bing

Japanese people who are familiar with our country's situation and can speak our language are often called "China experts." Thus, our country imitated it, and the term "Japan expert" was born. "Expert" is not a bad name. As far as individuals are concerned, it is only necessary to adhere to being fair and selfless. As far as undertakings are concerned, it belongs to communication. Whether it is related to international or domestic affairs, the word "expert" has greater significance. However, today, "expert" is also difficult to define. There are those who are experts through party affiliation, and there are those who should not be experts but cannot be experts. Weighing carefully, the authorities should pay attention to these three points.

Japan forcibly seized the Northeast, creating the puppet state of Manchukuo. The whole country is indignant and grieved. However, according to the facts, the international relations between China and Japan still exist; the international trade between China and Japan also continues unabated. Even though there are occasional trade deficits, our country's export volume also reaches six to seven million yuan per month. Communication is naturally busy due to trade needs. In addition, regarding diplomatic and private telegrams, according to historical statistics, there has also been an increase. In the past, the telegraph business was conducted through submarine cables, and the rights were not independent, and the profits mostly flowed overseas. Since our country's international radio station has been actively expanding, and in accordance with the prescribed steps, it has already communicated with various European and American countries one after another, only with Japan has it not been realized, which is somewhat ill-considered. Moreover, China and Japan have established a government-run Shanghai-Nagasaki submarine cable for communication, with a solid foundation. Even if this radio circuit is not completed, Japan will not be severely damaged, but we will suffer losses. Now that we have signed a contract, and the rights are in our own hands, then telegrams sent to Japan by our government and merchants can all be transmitted through our own international telegraph network. Developing international communication under independent sovereignty and increasing the national treasury revenue, then the wireless radio "Japan expert" has its own necessity to be an "expert", and it is not being an expert through party affiliation.

As of now, the international radio station is connected to twelve places worldwide. The United States, Germany, France, and Russia were connected previously, and the British and Japanese circuits were connected later. It is now being tested with Italy, and formal opening is expected soon. One connection and everything is connected, for all countries, and also for Japan. Therefore, from the perspective of the principles and position of international communication, the recent radio Japan expert is no different from the US, France, Germany, and Russia experts before this year, the British expert in February of this year, and the Italy expert that will be connected soon. It cannot be discussed together with the issues of opening traffic and mail with the puppet state of Manchukuo that have attracted social attention.

Telegraph Business Inspectors and the Public

— Kai

Our country's telegraph business has been established for more than fifty years, but compared with various European and American countries and neighboring Japan, the degree of its widespread development is still far behind! The reasons why it is not developed and not widespread are of course very complicated; such as the national level of knowledge is too low, the habit of sending telegrams has not been cultivated, the price of telegrams is too high, exceeding the economic capacity of the general public, coupled with frequent civil wars, commercial depression, official telegrams are rampant, clogging the lines, etc., are major reasons why telegrams cannot be developed, and the deep-rooted corruption and bureaucratic habits of the telegraph business itself have also been an obstacle to the evolution of telegrams. The authorities are aware of this, and deeply know that if we want to develop and popularize the telegraph business, we must first reform the telegraph business itself, we must thoroughly eradicate all the corrupt and official habits in the telecommunications world, and actively revitalize it. Therefore, recent measures and reforms are proceeding step by step towards commercialization and popularization. The authorities also believe that if we only seek internal rectification and reform, and do not maintain frequent contact and communication with the public, and the public still maintains the same indifferent attitude towards the telegraph business as before, then there will still be many barriers and resistance to the future development of the telegraph business. Therefore, in various busy bureaus and stations, the position of telegraph business inspector has been created. They go out to inquire, promote, and explain every day, to make practical connections with the public, as a model for improving business. Therefore, the establishment of telegraph business inspectors by telegraph bureaus and stations, from the perspective of facilitating the public and developing business, does have profound significance and important mission. Since telegraph business inspectors are set up to facilitate the public and promote business, their duties are also based on this principle, and have detailed regulations:

(1) If senders and receivers do not understand the various provincial fee methods or regulations and procedures for sending telegrams, they should be answered in detail one by one.

(2) If senders and receivers have any delays or errors in incoming and outgoing telegrams, they should be assisted in checking and investigating, so that senders and receivers can get a satisfactory reply.

(3) If senders and receivers have any dissatisfaction with the telegraph bureau: such as incoming reports not being translated, the transcription is not clear, fees are charged in violation of regulations, telegram deliverers demand gratuities, etc., they can be fully revealed, and the inspectors should report them to the bureau and station in a timely manner, so that they can be improved or banned.

(4) If senders and receivers have any opinions on what the bureau and station should improve or reform, they can make suggestions to them, and the inspectors should sincerely accept them, convey them to the authorities, and consider adopting and implementing them.

(5) If senders and receivers need various telegram regulations, telegram price lists, and delivery slips, they should be provided as much as possible.

(6) If senders and receivers do not understand Cyva (namely the International Radio Station), the station's founding process, content, and handling of matters should be explained in detail, so that they can understand the truth about the International Radio Station.

In short, the various barriers between the public and the telegram bureau and station in the past should be clarified and understood through the inspector's visits and explanations, and the various shortcomings of the telegraph bureau and station in the past should be thoroughly investigated by the inspector, so that they can be improved day by day. Therefore, those who are telegraph business inspectors should thoroughly understand the nature of their own duties and the importance of the mission they bear, work hard and diligently, and do their best in their duties. Whether when inquiring and promoting to businesses, organizations, groups, and individuals, the attitude must be humble and gentle, the words must be sincere, the answers must be detailed and clear, the suggestions must be sincerely accepted, and every effort must be made to ensure that the people sending and receiving telegrams get a good image invisibly. On the side of the public sending and receiving telegrams, they should also deeply understand that the telegraph business inspectors are beneficial to the public and not harmful at all. Whenever they come to inquire, they should provide them with various conveniences, so that they can fulfill their mission. In this way, the telegraph business can only achieve the true goals of commercialization and popularization with the help of the public.

Research on Shortwave Radio Applications (3)

— Wang Dachun

In shortwave radio telephone communication, sometimes the power is found to decrease due to excessively long communication distances. This is because the transmitting power on the line should be increased, especially when the transmitter is used for long distances. If the transmitting power is maintained at the original level, the transmission efficiency will inevitably be weakened. In ordinary very long-wave radio telephones, only about 10% to 15% of the actual power on the antenna is radiated. However, for shorter waves of 15 meters, the power radiated by the antenna often reaches 70%. From this perspective, for example, if the power of a long-wave transmitter is 300 kilowatts (kW), the power supplied to the antenna will be 150 kilowatts, but the actual radiated power is only 17 kilowatts. In the case of shortwaves, if the power is 30 kilowatts and the antenna requires 10 kilowatts, the radiated power can still reach 7 kilowatts. If the antenna of this shortwave machine is directional, all the radiated waves are concentrated in one direction, and the magnitude of its power is self-evident.

The use of shortwaves in radio can greatly increase the number of communication circuits. This is one of the reasons why shortwaves can be widely and practically used. Consider the following example: Suppose a relatively long wave has a frequency band of 50 to 100 kilocycles per second. Even if the width of each frequency band is reduced to 2,200 cycles (which is the minimum limit in commercial radio), and all the frequency transmission power is squeezed together, leaving almost no space between the frequency bands, the number of effective communication circuits obtained still cannot exceed 25. If shortwaves are used, according to modern experimental results, within the frequency range of 6,000 to 12,000 kilocycles per second, using 200 circuits of radio telephone, the spacing between each transmitting frequency band can still be 30 kilocycles per second. If this spacing is reduced to 10 kilocycles per second, the available radio telephone circuits can be increased threefold, for a total of 600 circuits. This is factually possible and is a point of progress in shortwaves.

In trivial detail, I have compiled this short article. The advantages and disadvantages of shortwave radio communication seem to have been discussed in detail. Originally, radio wave transmission is ever-changing. Shortwaves have not yet reached perfection. Improving them to be entirely beneficial and without any disadvantages is not something that can be achieved overnight. However, with the omnipotence of modern science, future progress can be expected day by day.

Telecommunications Lines

— Jiran

Telecommunications—excluding radio telegraphs and telephones—rely on lines and machinery to form electrical connections and realize the transmission of telecommunications, whether telegraph or telephone. Machinery belongs to the internal workings. How are they constructed? How are they managed? How do they operate? It is not easy for the general public to understand the gist without visiting the equipment within the bureau. As for the lines, they pass through city streets, rural fields, and along motorways and railways. The stately erected, winding lines are visible everywhere. We are accustomed to them and do not find them odd, considering these utility poles and wires to be merely communication tools. However, if we think about it carefully, on this single thin wire, various symbolic currents flow intermittently every second, or various talking currents flicker and fluctuate, constantly flowing and going back and forth. If radio waves could be made visible, one would see currents of different lengths, carrying the mission of communication, alternating and direct, flowing on these tiny wires. The speed is beyond description. In short, compared with the transmission of various kinds of energy, the speed of "electricity" is only second to "light".

Telecommunications lines can be roughly divided into overhead lines, underground lines, and submarine lines. Underground and submarine lines use cables, while overhead lines use bare wires as well as cables. In general, lines that are supported and raised in the air are called overhead. The lines erected can also be called open wires (i.e., bare wires), because they are clear and easily visible, and are clearly distinguished from the wires in cables that are covered with an outer layer.

Building telecommunications lines (including telegraphs and telephones) on land using cables is quite common in the United States. For example, when two cities are not far apart, long-distance telephone lines are often laid using cables instead of open wires. If the line is over a thousand miles long, unless the number of required wires exceeds what one pole can bear, open wires are generally used for communication. The reason is that cables are more expensive and labor costs are much higher. From an economic perspective, open wires are certainly more advantageous. Although China's telecommunications industry has a history of more than fifty years, except for submarine cables used in some areas along the coast and the Yangtze River, and overhead or underground cables used for urban telephones, most long-distance land communications use overhead open wires.

When lines pass through rivers, lakes, and seas, where there is no possibility of detouring, it is undoubtedly necessary to use submarine cables. However, for long-distance communications across the mainland, unless required by the business, open wires are mostly preferred. The United States is the most developed country in telephone communications. Therefore, underground cables are used to connect New York to Philadelphia, Washington, and other important cities across the western continent. This is because the need for telephone lines has surged, and the number of circuits is beyond what poles can bear, as mentioned above. In practical terms, burying cables deep underground can avoid the impact of wind and snow disasters, and save on routine maintenance costs. However, once a problem occurs, excavation and repair are time-consuming and costly, unlike open wires, which can be quickly repaired by patrolling along the route as soon as a problem is discovered.

The above has roughly explained the composition of lines, but there is still something more to be said. In Europe and the United States, there is a growing trend to abandon open wires in favor of cables, especially in cities. Within cities, lines crisscross, with electric lights, trams, and so on scattered everywhere, which is detrimental to the appearance of the city and often dangerous. The only solutions are to bury the lines deep underground (i.e., underground cables) or to suspend them in cable form (i.e., overhead cables). Moreover, the development of long-distance telephones is progressing rapidly. Due to the increase in telephone circuits, there is a general sense of the need for cables, and manufacturing companies are further exploring and researching to perfect them. In recent years, experts have made inventions such as amplification equipment to amplify the sound of telephones, and radio wave transmission to increase transmission efficiency. The use of cables has become widespread, and the adoption of trunk lines has become more frequent. In countries with developed telecommunications, open wires are considered outdated. However, considering the current state of development in China, the use of cables is not yet essential. This is due to the different circumstances and should not be generalized.

The Relationship Between Public Cooperation and the Telephone Industry

— Wang Qikun

The nature of the telephone industry is that of a transportation enterprise for the nation, and a public utility for the locality. The completion of its mission and the development of its business depend on the efforts of the operating organization, but also require public cooperation and maintenance to fully achieve its goals. The term "public" includes all telephone users, including military and government agencies. Taking the capital as an example, the relationship between the telephone industry and the public is described below.

(1) Finance

Since the telephone business is state-owned, its funding should be raised by the state. However, when the state is facing financial difficulties, if the public needs telephones, they should share the burden and provide financial assistance so that the industry can be expanded as soon as possible. In this way, the public can also benefit earlier, with considerable gains. In Japan, during the Great Earthquake of 1923, almost all telephones in Tokyo and Yokohama were destroyed. Due to financial constraints, only the telephones of old subscribers could be restored on schedule, with no resources left for expansion. However, the number of requests for telephone installation increased annually, making it difficult to reject them all. Therefore, an alternative solution had to be found, with new subscribers bearing the construction costs. Later, a bill was enacted by the Diet, recognizing telephones as the assets of the subscribers, which could be bought and sold at will. However, new subscribers had to pay an engineering fee of 1,500 Japanese yen for each telephone installed. Furthermore, because the restoration and expansion projects of the telephone bureau were numerous and large-scale, it was difficult to install all new subscribers at the same time. Each year, only a portion could be accommodated, with public lotteries held regularly. Only those who won the lottery could pay the fee and have their phones installed, thus eliminating the need to find ways to purchase a line. Qingdao, China, also imitated this method, with the engineering fee set at 235 yuan, resulting in higher revenue for the telephone bureau and easier expansion. In the capital, the telephone bureau has three branches in addition to Pukou, with a capacity of 3,000 numbers at the main branch. All numbers were already filled, making it impossible to add more. Therefore, it was decided to establish a new South Branch, initially installing equipment for 2,000 numbers, and a suitable site has been purchased. However, due to financial constraints, the expansion has had to be delayed slightly, a difficult situation that seems to be understood by the public.

Secondly, let's consider Japan again. While the government is working hard to expand telephone services, its financial resources are ultimately limited. The telephone budget must be approved by the Diet, allowing for the establishment of new bureaus in only a limited number of locations each year. The public's need for telephones is urgent, making it difficult to ignore. Therefore, a special telephone installation method was established. If the public in a certain area wishes to establish a special telephone bureau ahead of the national budget, they can jointly submit a petition, and the government will plan everything. All required labor and material costs are borne by the petitioners and contributed to the state, with no compensation before or after. However, long-distance telephone connections from that area to the rest of the country will be built by the state (which, of course, must be included in the budget beforehand). In contrast, in China, due to financial constraints, the Ministry of Communications cannot actively expand long-distance telephone services within cities. Provinces are therefore establishing their own services. Thus, the same telephone business is contributed to the state in Japan without compensation, while in China, there are those belonging to the local government and those belonging to the central government, with different prices and systems. The Japanese criticize China for being disorganized, and while there may be an intention to defame, we should reflect on ourselves. Furthermore, subscribers have the right to use the telephone, which implies the obligation to pay fees. In Western countries, subscribers pay the rental fees in advance, recognizing that obligations should precede rights, and that telephone rental fees are no different from taxes if the telephone service is operated by the state. In China, only subscribers in Qingdao pay the rental fee three months in advance at the telephone bureau at the beginning of each quarter. In other regions, the bureau sends staff to collect the fees, which often results in arrears. While this may be due to the lack of effort or misconduct of the collectors, if subscribers could embrace a spirit of cooperation and voluntarily pay the fees at the bureau, not only could the number of collectors be reduced, but also the potential for corruption could be prevented. Since postage and telegram fees must be paid at the bureau, telephone fees could also be paid in this way.

(2) Usage

Whether telephone subscribers use the service appropriately has a significant impact on the satisfaction of the telephone industry's services. No matter how comprehensive the equipment of the telephone bureau is, it has certain limitations, especially in the case of automatic systems. If subscribers use the service without restraint, the supply will not be able to meet the demand, and both the telephone bureau and the subscribers will suffer. The points that subscribers should pay attention to when using the telephone are described below:

1. The subscriber's number is listed in the directory. Starting this year, the Ministry of Communications has ordered all telephone bureaus to print correction slips for subscribers who have installed, removed, moved, or changed their names, once a month, to facilitate verification. However, the numbers of newly installed subscribers may not be included, so the telephone bureau has an information desk to assist subscribers with inquiries. In the capital, it is customary for the public not to check the directory before making a call, but instead to ask the information desk to check the number. This has led to an unexpected increase in unnecessary calls, occupying the lines and hindering legitimate calls. If subscribers could consider the overall situation and take the trouble to consult the directory, it would only require a small effort.

2. When subscribers move, they often allow others to use their telephone without transferring the account. The new users, in turn, often try to save trouble and money by not reporting the transfer for a long time, so the directory still lists the old subscriber's name. If someone wants to reach the new user, they cannot find the number in the directory, and the information desk cannot provide the correct information. The caller may mistakenly think that the information desk is not providing good service, which affects its reputation, and the caller's business with the subscriber is also delayed, harming both parties.

3. The telephone bureau has limited equipment, so not all subscribers can talk at the same time, at most only 20-30%. If subscribers engage in lengthy and irrelevant conversations, they not only occupy the lines for a long time and hinder others' legitimate calls, but also prevent important calls from being received from other locations, harming both themselves and others. During peak telephone hours (e.g., 10:00 AM to 1:00 PM and 3:00 PM to 4:00 PM), it is especially important to avoid unnecessary calls.

(3) Lines

Telephone lines are located along the roadside. Due to financial constraints, it is impossible to assign people to patrol and guard them, so it relies on the military police and the public to maintain them. If there is any theft or damage, the telephone bureau should be notified promptly so that repairs can be made quickly to facilitate communication. As for telephone poles and wires set up on private land, this is a last resort. If local residents consider it to be a hindrance, they can request that it be moved, or demand compensation. Article 18 of the Telecommunications Conditions promulgated by the National Government on August 5, 1929, stipulates: "State-owned telecommunications organizations may choose convenient locations for the construction of lines, regardless of where they pass. However, if it obstructs the rights of private individuals, the injured party may request compensation after the Ministry of Communications of the Executive Yuan of the National Government or its entrusted agency has verified the facts." Long-distance telephone and telegraph poles, with the exception of a very small number, are all planted on private land, which inevitably obstructs crops. However, the public understands the importance of the telecommunications business and embraces a spirit of sacrificing private interests for the public good, and has never requested this compensation. In Japan, it is stipulated that a rental fee of one cent per year should be paid for each telephone pole planted on private land, but no one has ever asked the government for this rental fee. Recently, the Capital Telephone Bureau received a bizarre warning letter, stating that today, the bureau installed a telephone for Mr. Zhang ××'s residence, and the wires passed through Mr. Wei ××'s land and occupied more than three zhang of airspace. Although the writer is from Sheng County, Zhejiang, and is unfamiliar with Nanjing, he is still a member of the Republic of China. He warned the bureau about this organized infringement on his property and demanded a response within three days, otherwise he would seek judicial and administrative solutions. This gentleman equated the lines of the state-owned telecommunications organization with the Japanese military aircraft that illegally flew through North China's airspace, a distortion that does not need to be refuted. It is regrettable that the bourgeoisie of the capital cannot recognize the nature of telephone lines and are unwilling to cooperate and maintain them. It is reminiscent of the burning of telephone poles by the public in Hunan and other provinces due to feng shui concerns when telegraphs were first introduced to China five thousand years ago. Furthermore, the majority of long-distance telephone and telegraph lines pass through the outskirts of cities, and even in remote rural areas. The surveying markers and the poles and wires after construction are almost all located on private land. If the cooperation of the landowners cannot be obtained, there is a risk of being attacked and it will be impossible to fulfill their mission.

Based on the three points mentioned above, the importance of public cooperation to the telephone business is clear. Since the development of telephones is related to the public interest, the public will surely cooperate. The more developed the telephone, the more public cooperation is needed, and the more the public cooperates, the more the telephone can develop. These two things are mutually causative and mutually beneficial. If we seek the development of the telephone business, this is what we hope for from the public, and it is imperative.

Talking About Wooden Poles for Telecommunications (1)

— Gan

There are several types of telephone poles: wooden poles, iron poles, and concrete poles. Among them, wooden poles are the cheapest and most widely used, so I will start by describing wooden poles.

The materials used for wooden poles on telegraph and telephone lines also vary. In the United States, fir, chestnut, and red pine are used. In general, the United States has rich forests, and materials are sourced locally to save on transportation costs. Therefore, red pine is mostly used for lines west of the Rocky Mountains, while fir and chestnut are more abundant in the eastern states and the Midwest, and the above two types are used for pole harvesting. Relatively speaking, fir is preferred by most countries for pole materials because it grows slowly and the trunks are straight, making it suitable for the installation of electrical lines. Chestnut wood is often curved, making it less aesthetically pleasing than fir in urban areas. However, it has one advantage: fir is prone to cracking when dry, while chestnut wood is not. Ordinary electric poles erected in densely populated areas are often exposed to smoke and become brittle, but chestnut wood can withstand it without harm. Also, when pole wood catches fire, chestnut wood has strong resistance due to its firm inner quality, and it is slower and more resistant to burning than other types of wood. This is certainly an advantage. In European countries, where timber production is not high, some is imported from the Americas in addition to self-sufficiency. The wooden poles used that are produced in this continent are only from Scandinavia, Finland, and part of Soviet Russia. They are mostly red pine; however, Siberia has extremely rich forests, and many are suitable for telephone poles. Over the years, large quantities have been sold to Northeast China and within the customs, which is what is known as Huanghua pine. In China, timber is mostly planted in the inland provinces of Guangxi, Hunan, Jiangxi, Fujian and other provinces, and large quantities of timber are sold to other places every year. In particular, Hankou is the national center, where timber merchants gather. Most of the wooden poles used for telecommunications are sourced from Hankou, and are rarely purchased from overseas unless absolutely necessary. China's telecommunications materials, from machinery to electrical wires and parts, are mostly supplied by other countries. Due to the decline of industry and the lack of manufacturing capacity, the leakage is very large, and there is still no way to reverse it. Only this wooden pole, compared with imported goods, is not inferior, and is used by the general telecommunications workers, like the only remaining fruit. Touching upon this, I cannot help but sigh. However, from the perspective of telecommunications alone, the number of wooden poles required each year is already huge. According to US statistics, there are more than 35 million telephone poles nationwide. Assuming that the average lifespan of a wooden pole is ten years, then one-tenth must be replaced each year, which requires 3.5 million wooden poles. According to a survey of China's telecommunications in 1931, as of the end of 1930, there were 175,873 li of lines, and the number of poles was 1,187,934. If we use the United States as a ratio, we would need to replace more than 118,000 poles annually. If China's afforestation efforts are not improved, then the poles needed for telecommunications will be cut down day by day, and it may be difficult to sustain. What's more, the suppliers who rely on timber are countless. Although Dr. Sun Yat-sen advocated afforestation for more than one reason, even if we think of it from the telecommunications use, it should arouse the attention of society.

Telecommunications World

— Zhenfang

New Construction of Telecommunications in Soviet Russia

February 25th marked the 13th anniversary of the establishment of the Georgian Soviet system. The wireless telephone between Tiflis and Moscow (3,218 kilometers) has been completed and officially opened for business. Before this month, shortwave photo wireless telephone between Moscow and Tashkent (3,328 kilometers) began to work. This is the first long-distance communication established in the Soviet Union and one of the longest circuits in the world. This year, the telegraph and telephone line between Moscow and Boli is under construction, with a length of 9,000 kilometers, exceeding the distance from New York to San Francisco. The new line will pass through Samarra, Boli, Irkutsk, Chita, and other places. The electrical connection line from Boli to Vladivostok, Amur Province, and Yakutsk Province is also planned. In order to increase the volume, it is planned to build 30 special amplification stations.

Opening of Osaka Wharf Telephone

The wharf telephone service of Osaka Port connecting ship shore was established on February 15. Because the distance between the wharf and the commercial center is quite far, the installation of telephones is very needed. The telephone bill is 5 yen per day, but there is no additional fee for calls within the city. The long-distance telephone fee is charged at the normal price. When Osaka ships are docked, there is no wireless telephone installed between the ship and the shore like Kobe. That business,

Promotion of French Fax Telegraph

According to a notice from the British Post Office: the fax telegraph business between Britain and France has now been extended to the cities and towns in the provinces of Bordeaux, Lyon, Mabaud, Nice, and Pistertrasbourg. After that, the transmission of pictures from France to England only needs to be transferred through the Paris Central Telegraph Office.

Closure of Famous British Radio Station

The Poldhu radio station in Cornwall, England, is scheduled to close at the end of this month. The release of this notice aroused a group of attention. The station was the station where Marconi received the first transatlantic Morse signal in Newfoundland, and it was also the station where the first wireless telephone was transmitted from England to the United States. Now, due to centralized research, there is no need to use this old-fashioned radio station.

Amendment to Telegraph Prices by US Commercial Telegraph Companies

US commercial telegraph companies have successively announced that, starting this year, they will implement various international telegraph prices revised by the Madrid International Telegraph Conference. The original ten-character codewords have been changed to five-character codewords - charged at 60% of the ordinary telegraph price. The express telegraph price was charged at three times the ordinary telegraph price, but now it has been changed to two times the ordinary telegraph price. In addition, priority telegrams traveling to and from both sides of the Atlantic Ocean are charged at 25% of the ordinary telegraph price, but now all are charged at the express telegram price. The priority telegram price was only applicable to telegrams between the United States and European countries, and those traveling to and from other countries were called express telegrams. The revised price cancels the priority telegram method. According to general observations, international remittances and stock trading between the United States and London, Paris, Amsterdam, Berlin, etc. will be greatly affected, because the original US priority telegrams were mostly issued by exchanges and banks.

Bi-Monthly News

— Club Member

Revised Method for Radio Material Import Passport

The Ministry of Communications believes that the original "Method for Temporary Import Passports for Radio Materials" is not perfect, and has now been revised to "Method for Applying for Import Passports for Radio Materials," which has been submitted to the Executive Yuan and approved by the Fumu government. The differences between this method and the old temporary method are recorded below:

1. For imported materials that belong to radio receiving products, a long application form should be filled out and submitted to the ministry, along with the shipping invoice and three copies of it.

2. For imported materials that belong to transmitting products, in addition to the previous article, the purpose should be described in detail. If the order is placed on behalf of someone else, a certificate of purpose from the person ordering the food should be attached.

3. When transmitting products are sold, the selling merchant should obtain a statement from the buyer and submit it to the Ministry for verification and issuance of a permit before selling.

4. Passport fee is calculated according to the value of the material, excluding the fee.

Detailed methods can be requested from our company by letter.

Public Telephones will be installed in Post and Telecommunications Bureaus

In order to facilitate public telephone calls, the Ministry of Communications has recently formulated a method for setting up public telephones in telecommunications bureaus and post offices, ordering the post and telecommunications bureaus in large commercial ports that have municipal or remote telephone services run by the Ministry to install public telephones so that they can retail municipal or long-distance telephone calls. This method can be realized in the near future, and the public can make calls anytime, anywhere, which will be extremely convenient.

Supplement to the Shanghai Daily Local News

Talks

A True Man Does Not Eat Food of a False Nation

— Mingtang

Yesterday, I saw in the newspaper that Deng Tiemei, the Commander-in-Chief of the Liaoning Self-Defense Army, after being captured, was escorted by over a thousand Japanese soldiers to the Shenyang Army Prison for detention. A small Japanese squad guarded him. Officials of the puppet government and Japanese individuals who admired Deng's reputation flocked to visit him. Deng only spoke with one or two individuals who possessed some integrity and remained silent otherwise. He has not eaten for several days since entering the prison. The Japanese sent several tables of banquets, but he refused to eat, saying, "A true man does not eat food of a false nation." He directly rebuked the puppet officials for their shameless treachery, causing those who heard him to feel ashamed and avert their faces. This is truly a precious and moving piece of news that should fill us with awe and make us feel increasingly ashamed.

The spirit of the Chinese people has long been declining. Since September 18th, Japan has used artillery fire to force the entire country to submit. At that time, there were indeed some impassioned students and small citizens who made some displays of defiance, but these were soon completely extinguished. As for now, the term "anti-Japanese" is almost never heard, and everyone seems to be quietly living under oppression. Debauchery and pleasure fill every city. Many people observe that with the spirit of the Chinese people so diminished, China is completely without hope. In reality, this is completely wrong. How could the spirit of the Chinese people have declined? Not only has it not declined, but it is secretly, at the core of society, growing and developing day by day. Responding to the impetus of objective external facts, it is becoming increasingly urgent and progressive. Deng Tiemei's impassioned vow not to eat the food of a false nation, although it is his personal action, immediately reveals to me countless tens of thousands of anti-Japanese people in the entire Northeast behind him.

The anti-Japanese actions of the entire Northeast anti-Japanese populace did not begin today. Since September 18th, they have started an unprecedented bloody struggle, following the oppression of imperialist guns. This struggle has reached an even more intense and acute stage today. We should not think that just because we haven't seen news about the Northeast Volunteer Armies for a long time, the anti-Japanese forces of the Northeast populace have been extinguished. This is wrong.

Do not be pessimistic, the anti-resistance forces of China will not be destroyed, and will never be destroyed.

Cousin

— Jun

After a separation of ten years, my cousin suddenly returned home, appearing much older. The image of my cousin from ten years ago is completely different from the way she looks now. I couldn't help but sigh secretly: youth is fleeting, my cousin has truly aged!

I remember when she was young, she often came to stay at my house. At that time, she was a girl of seventeen or eighteen, while I was only about ten years old. She was very beautiful, as beautiful as a cherished lily about to bloom. Among the many female relatives, almost no one could compare to her. From a young age, people called her "Beauty." Even now, I still call her "Sister Beauty." She was very loving and caring towards me, always touching my hair and taking me out to play. I also felt very gentle and affectionate towards her. Because she was so beautiful and had no siblings, my parents cherished her very much, regarding her as the apple of their eye. In particular, regarding the matter of marriage, they were not easily accommodating. On the one hand, they hoped to choose a suitable match for their daughter, and on the other hand, they were reluctant to let her leave their side. Therefore, whenever this matter was mentioned, they would say to choose slowly, to choose slowly, delaying it.

Later, I left home to wander outside and never went back, but soon I finally heard the news of my cousin's marriage.

This time when I returned home, my cousin happened to be there too, giving us the chance to meet. However, my cousin was no longer the cousin of the past. She had become the mother of a four-month-old child. Her face was vaguely marked with many wrinkles, and her eyebrows knitted together when she smiled. The color of youth had completely faded, leaving not a trace, and the vitality of her youth was forever separated from her. The accumulation of time and the tribulations of life had caused her to lose everything, causing her to quickly wither. A sense of life's melancholy and sorrow was strongly expressed in her actions and speech. The fragrant and youthful period of a young woman had passed like a dream.

What a middle-aged mother-like cousin!

The burden of managing her son and all the trivial family matters was heavily pressed on her shoulders, making her senses strangely dull. She had become like a machine, working tirelessly from morning to night, without a moment to rest. Her four or five children were always making trouble, either arguing about food or drink, or one crying and the other screaming, pacifying the older ones, while the younger ones cling to her, keeping her hands and feet constantly busy.

Every day was so exhausting that her bones felt numb. At night, the fatigue of the whole day made her feel unbearably sleepy. She would hastily lie on the bed, preparing to sleep comfortably. But then the children would start clamoring again: wanting water, wanting candy. If she pretended not to care, the children would hit their mother's body, insisting on waking her up.

In this situation, my cousin had no choice but to temporarily stay with relatives for a few days to seek peace and quiet, and my house was where she liked to come, freeing her from the chores of her own home for a while. But the children's entanglements came along with her.

Page 22

In the morning, I saw my cousin baring her chest, breastfeeding an infant less than a year old. She was also putting on makeup in front of the mirror. The infant was probably uncomfortable lying on her bent knees, and although she was drinking, she was still acting strangely, struggling desperately. The mother had no choice but to put down her hand, pick her up and shake her a few times, and then stuff another nipple into her mouth. The child still cried hoarsely. So my cousin became annoyed, slapped the child's bottom forcefully, and cursed:

"You little bastard, cry yourself to death, die early and be done with it!"

"Cousin, the child doesn't understand anything. Hitting her won't help. Just coax her gently." I said softly from the side.

"You don't understand. These short-lived things seem like enemies from a previous life, deliberately coming to collect debts. I'm really fed up."

In this way, I discovered that my cousin's temperament had changed greatly. Usually, whenever she was in a bad mood, and the child happened to be bothering her, she would grab her and slap her a few times, seemingly using this to vent her anger. Mothers often like to do this, unable to bear the anger from their husbands or mothers-in-law, and having no way to vent it, so they take it out on their children. My cousin had also developed this kind of temper!

Thorns

— Yan Wei

Every step is a thorn, and this is another experience.

In the morning, the sky was so gloomy, it was the season of plum rains, and it looked like it was going to rain. My wife and I didn't bring rain gear, and we were afraid of getting our new clothes wet, so we chose two casual outfits and took the train from our hometown, Cixi, to Shanghai.

We, who are used to a pampered life in the city, could not withstand a month of roaming under the sun, and our skin had turned much darker. Because we ran in the mountains every day, we didn't have time to get haircuts, so our hair had grown quite a bit. Reluctantly, we bid farewell to the mountains and rivers of our hometown. The train took us past village after village, and as we listlessly watched the scenery shift, we couldn't help but feel a special emotion.

The train stopped at XX Station. In the crowded crowd, we were挤 squeezed out of the station. Just as we were about to call for a car, soldiers in military uniforms stopped us. The soldiers wore multi-pointed badges on their arms, and alarmingly, they carried wooden guns with exposed blades on their shoulders. Their chests were covered in various miscellaneous items, in short, frightening weapons that could destroy us.

The soldier said, "Open them!" and pointed with his hand.

Under the soldier's command, I began to realize how small my life was, and only then did I realize that the warrior wanted to see the suitcase in my hand. I solemnly placed the suitcase I was carrying on the ground. Just then, the warrior ordered again:

"Hurry up!"

Panicked, I was so eager that I couldn't even open the lock. After a commotion, I finally managed to open it, but the soldier's expression was no longer pleasant. He perfunctorily flipped through the clothes, and didn't care about the documents or newspapers. Instead, he repeatedly examined the packages of food that our relatives had sent us. To put it in merchant terms, it was like a Jiangxi jeweler looking at antiques. What he considered most suspicious was a bag of peeled longan meat.

"What is this?"

"Longan meat!"

He seemed not to believe it, took out a few pieces, and ordered me to taste a few. Seeing that I didn't suffer any pain, he thought it was safe to try, and chewed some too. But once he tasted the flavor, it was all over. He grabbed a large handful and stuffed it into his mouth. My business was finished. I looked for my wife. My wife also had a suitcase ready to be opened.

But women's things are naturally more miscellaneous. He found a treasure trove, looked at this item, and then that item. I started to get a little angry. So I mustered up my courage:

"Could you please hurry up and find out what's what!"

"What did you say?"

I saw that the situation was not right, and quickly shut up.

Unexpectedly, there was also a suspicious item in my wife's suitcase, a package of Chinese medicine called Plague Averting Pills.

As usual, we were interrogated. I told him what it was. He wanted to call me again, but he was a little embarrassed. I told him it was medicine, but he didn't believe me. This was difficult.

"Okay," this posture was different again, probably meaning to keep the case, and look for something else. He searched around like a hunting dog.

Ah! The warrior's behavior stopped. There was a package of letters, one of which was a letter from a friend asking an important person to forward it to us. He looked at the envelope for a while, and then pointed to the name of the important person, asking if I knew him? He probably thought that if the important person could forward the letter, this person must have some background. So he closed the suitcase, threw back the Plague Averting Pills, and said, "Finished."

We walked out of the station in a panic.

Every step is a thorn, and this is another experience.

Zongzi Talk

— A Ping

The Chinese are a barbaric people and don't know what art is. However, in addition to cooking raw rice into cooked rice, they can also wrap it in bamboo leaves and fill it with lard and bean paste, red beans, and meat bones to make a multi-angled zongzi, as it is called. The zongzi from Sijing is the most famous. During the Dragon Boat Festival, major local product companies promote themselves as the Zongzi King. The most luxurious ones sell for six yuan. Country people mistakenly believe that Shanghai is paved with gold, or this is due to this kind of exaggerated rumor. But the customs of eating cherries and green plums at the Beginning of Summer, eating mooncakes at the Mid-Autumn Festival, and eating zongzi at the Dragon Boat Festival, the former can be said to be new products on the market, eat them quickly; the latter are indeed somewhat mythological and absurd. Even the dragon boat races have become good advertisements for selling more tickets. This clearly shows that the Chinese are good at exploiting the reputation of the dead. Just look at the fact that the bones of the deceased are not yet cold, and their posthumous works have already been promoted with great skill.

Since I arrived in Shanghai, I ordered a ban on unconscious sacrifices, so I was judged guilty of "extinguishing ancestors." Of course, leisurely pleasures like eating mooncakes and eating zongzi are not included in the account after eating enough white rice. Last year on the Dragon Boat Festival, a girlfriend personally sent several zongzi, saying that "if you don't eat zongzi on the Dragon Boat Festival, no one will send you any when you're old." She is a university student and should have read more books than me, or perhaps it is in line with scientific principles, so I devoured the zongzi at noon that day. But according to unscientific sayings: "Accumulate grain to prevent hunger, raise children to prevent old age." To think that zongzi has the same effect as children is a mystery that I have never known in my life.

The Children After Their Father Died

— Yingying

The children had some doubts about their mother's unusual behavior recently; resentment – it seemed that their mother's current treatment of them was not as gentle and considerate as before. She often showed a fierce gaze; if it were a mistake in the past, it wouldn't make her angry! She wouldn't pull down their pants and start hitting them like now. Even if she corrected the mistake or taught them a lesson, they wouldn't do it again; it's not like now, where she hits their buttocks as soon as they make a move! It seems like a very skilled technique, after several practice experiences.

After being beaten for no apparent reason, the children cried for a while, with no one to complain to! They watched their mother dress up gaudily, put on new clothes, and go out. Before leaving the room, she even came back in again, looked in the mirror, applied rouge again, and then leaned close to the mirror several times to look at her face. It seemed like the two patches of red were not very even. She felt disappointed!

From the corner of the mirror, she saw the two children stopping their tears and peeking. She couldn't help but get angry again, rushed forward, and with both hands, grabbed the two children by their long ears.

"Mother, we won't do it again..."

In fact, the children didn't quite understand the reason why their mother pulled their ears this time.

Seeing that their mother had truly left the door, very far away, and they couldn't see her shadow!

The two children sat down side by side on the wooden bench, with two streams of dried tears on their faces and dark bruises where they had rubbed them with the back of their hands. The older one reached over and touched the ear of the younger one that had been pulled.

"Younger brother, does it still hurt?" The younger one didn't answer, and cried out again. He leaned into the older one's arms.

"Older brother, I really don't believe it, she's our mom, our own mother?"

The older brother held the younger brother's hand, the dark back of his hand where he had rubbed his eyes. He couldn't say anything? He didn't know when, a tear rolled down onto the younger brother's hand. "Ah, older brother, you're crying! Does your ear still hurt?" The younger brother jumped up! He had completely forgotten that he still had tears on his face too.

"It's not that my ear hurts! I'm wondering, why is mother so bad to us after father died? Could it be that because father died, mother can hit us; otherwise, just for moving a bowl of beans, we would be beaten so badly! Younger brother, how old is older brother this year? Yesterday, Uncle Zhang told me that mother is very close to Jin A-si from the village ahead! The one with the freckled and pockmarked face who smokes; she wants us to call him uncle. I didn't want to call him that, so mother twisted my lips until they were blue. That person is so annoying! But mother is so fond of him."

"Older brother, let's buy a pistol and shoot him dead!"

But the children still didn't have that much courage!

After the news of their mother's remarriage to Jin A-si was announced, the two children clung to their mother's clothes and wouldn't let go, crying as if the tears were coming from a burst water faucet.

Uncle Zhang couldn't bear to see it and went to Jin A-si's side to plead! Allow them to bring the two children! They didn't agree! The reason was that they already had too many children, and didn't need two more burdens.

And their mother was also determined to abandon these two children; she sold them to Old Man Chen for thirty yuan to look after the cattle and do odd jobs.

Afterwards, the images of the children faded and disappeared from their mother's memory.

Notes for Contributors

— Wu Qi

Do you know the criteria for submitting articles to magazines? I know a thing or two and don't dare to keep it a secret. Now I'm making it public.

Because readers are worshiping idols, magazine editors are pleased to sell the heads of savages: celebrities, scholars, PhDs, important people, and well-known writers. Articles from these people are very welcome, no matter how many articles from unknown people are piled up like mountains. They ask them for articles in person and also send letters urging them to submit. Some even ask others to intercede and help get an article. In this situation, articles submitted by unknown people are either returned unopened with postage stamps attached, or thrown into the wastebasket without postage stamps, sentenced to imprisonment. If you understand this situation, if you hope that your own masterpiece will be published, you should (1) discuss it with celebrities, scholars, PhDs, important people, and well-known writers, and submit the article with their brand. This will guarantee your success. But if the manuscript fee is only one to two yuan per thousand words when you submit it yourself and it is lucky enough to be published, but now it is submitted with a brand and is published, it is five to ten yuan per thousand words. Then you should obediently let the owner of the brand distribute the manuscript fee to you. Even if it is one to two yuan per thousand words, and he earns a lot without working, you have to endure it and not say anything. This is speaking about dissertations and literary creation. If it is a translation, then you should (2) discuss it with celebrities, scholars, PhDs, important people, and well-known writers, add their brand as "co-translator", and submit the article. This will also guarantee your success. But the manuscript fee or royalties for "co-translated" articles must be split with the owner of the brand, either 50/50 or 60/40. You should endure the distribution of the "co-translator" and not make any claims. And for both of the above methods, practitioners should "keep the secret strictly." If someone exposes you and publishes the truth, and the "co-translator" and the nominal author order you to come forward and declare that what people are publishing is a rumor, you have to do it respectfully. | Don't people know the way? Let me tell you all: the first shop to start this kind of transaction was a romance novel shop, followed by a drama expert shop, an XX research expert shop, and a somewhat "pushed" essay expert shop. | However, the boss of the last shop once bought manuscripts without paying, so it is best to sign a contract with him to avoid future disputes.
